Rabbi Zalman Levitin, leader of The Chabad House in Palm Beach. Mr. Deitsch died Saturday, April 15, 2017, the Shabbat of Passover, in Jerusalem. He was 64. Rabbi Deitsch had been in a coma since Oct. 8, 2016, when he was injured in an anti-Semitic attack in the central train station in the city of Zhitomir, Ukraine, said Rabbi Levitin. He was airlifted to a hospital in Israel and underwent surgeries. Four suspects were arrested in the beating and robbery. Rabbi Deitsch served as a Chabad-Lubavitch emissary in France and Israel and had resided in Caesarea, Israel. He would travel to Zhitomir &ldquo;to take care of the Jewish graves there, most notably the grave of Rabbi Shneur Zalman of Liadi (the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and founder of Chabad Chassidism) and lead hospitality and programming at the burial site for visitors,&rdquo; said Rabbi Levitin. Rabbi Deitsch is survived by his wife, Shterna Sara; and their 11 children, Menouha Friedland (Aubervilliers, France); Rabbi Shnieur Zalman Deitsch (Minsk, Russia); Chana Appelbaum (Migdal HaEmek, Israel); Rabbi Yisroel Deitsch (Jerusalem); Rabbi Levi Yitzchok Deitsch (Jerusalem), Yehudis Fradkin (Rechovot, Israel); Rabbi Yosef Eliyahu Deitsch (Krayot, Israel); and ShlomoYehuda, Shmuel, Yocheved and Dovber, all of Caesarea. He also is survived by three brothers, Rabbis Chaim Sholom Deitsch, Shneur Zalman Deitsch and Moshe Deitsch. \n<!-- map content:  Hundreds of red sneaker-clad feet covered the floor of the Meat Market at a reception to benefit Red Sneakers for Oakley. Merrill Debbs, Tatiana Platt and Maribel Alvarez were chairwomen for the evening, which included a hors d&rsquo;oeuvres, Veuve Clicquot champagne, the Meat Market&rsquo;s &lsquo;Red Hot Cocktails&rsquo; and a high-end silent auction. Platt, in a red dress to match her sneakers, enlisted her three kids to hand out red bracelets to arriving guests. &ldquo;We are saving lives,&rdquo; Platt said. &ldquo;Oakley&rsquo;s story has helped save another child&rsquo;s life through a better understanding of the symptoms of a severe reaction to food allergies.&rdquo; Red Sneakers For Oakley was founded by Robert and Merrill Debbs after their 11-year-old son Oakley died from a severe allergic reaction to nuts. Robert Debbs and Eric Lumb were chairmen. Proceeds from the night assist Red Sneakers for Oakley in its mission to raise awareness about food allergies and the dangers through education and outreach programs. \n<!-- map content:  When curator Ray Merritt proposed Photography of Place to the Palm Beach Photographic Centre, he didn&rsquo;t have beautiful scenery in mind. &ldquo;I didn&rsquo;t want to do a landscape or a travel show,&rdquo; he said. &ldquo;I wanted to do photography of place and include people and nature as generic motifs.&rdquo; The 24 photographers in the show approach the topic in disparate ways, ranging from Caleb Cain Marcus&rsquo; images of glaciers to Fern Berman&rsquo;s close-ups of weathered junk. The show mixes iconic photographers such as Eugene Atget and Robert Frank, with contemporary art photographers such as April Gornik and Sally Gall and amateurs most people have never heard of. &ldquo;There are a lot of great amateur photographers, but they don&rsquo;t have venues where they can show their work,&rdquo; Merritt said. The amateurs he&rsquo;s chosen are so good that &ldquo;I think people will be hard put to figure out who are the amateurs and who are the professionals,&rdquo; he said. Marcus is no amateur. His work has been featured in National Geographic&rsquo;s online photography journal Proof, and his 2012 book, A Portrait of Ice, was selected by the trade magazine Photo District News as one of the best photography books of the year. He traveled to Iceland to photograph glaciers and trekked the 1,500-mile length of the Ganges River in Bangladesh and India to capture his images in the show. &ldquo;I&rsquo;ve always been interested in the idea that air is not empty space,&rdquo; he said of his images of the Ganges, which can appear as ephemeral as a mirage. &ldquo;Air can have a presence and texture to it and somehow it can hold events in space and change the resonance of a place because of the people and what happened there.&rdquo; It can take as many as 30 proofs to achieve the effects he wants. In Iceland, he looked for glaciers with &ldquo;personality,&rdquo; he said. &ldquo;Glaciers have such personality. Some look like the rolling hills of Vermont and others more like the Rocky Mountains.&rdquo; For Gornik, who is married to figurative artist Eric Fischl, photography is mainly a tool for constructing her paintings and drawings. She&rsquo;s exhibited her art at major museums and has work currently touring in a show of Paul Allen&rsquo;s collection. The show at Palm Beach Photographic Centre is one of the first times she&rsquo;s shown her photographs. She shot the images during trips to Tanzania and Namibia. Her landscapes are often infused with a sense of mystery and unease. &ldquo;What&rsquo;s amazing about landscape is that it&rsquo;s the other in the most extreme way,&rdquo; she said. Her art is a means of locating herself in the universe and finding something meaningful within it. &ldquo;There&rsquo;s a difference between something that you can spiritually project into and something that&rsquo;s a nice picture,&rdquo; she said. Berman rarely shoots far from her home in coastal Connecticut. Her multiple sclerosis has curtailed trips such as the one to Morocco, where she photographed goat skins drying on a rooftop from a higher vantage point. She was attracted by the shape of the roofs and the skins&rsquo; yellow color, but &ldquo;I had to shoot with a bouquet of flowers in my hand because I couldn&rsquo;t stand the smell,&rdquo; she said. Today, she turns her lens on fragments of graffiti-splashed walls and decaying trucks. She prefers man-made subjects to nature. Her greatest influences are painters such as Franz Marc, Wassily Kandinsky and Mark Rothko.&rdquo;I love color and texture,&rdquo; she said. She shoots only film. &ldquo;I like limitations,&rdquo; she said. &ldquo;It makes me focus.&rdquo; Her disease has done that for her, too. &ldquo;I&rsquo;ve slowed down,&rdquo; she said. &ldquo;It&rsquo;s good for my photography. It makes me see more.&rdquo; If Merritt succeeds in his aim, visitors, too, will see more of the many ways that place can be portrayed. -->\n<article class=\"story cm-channel-story cm-story \n<!-- map content:  Registration has begun for the Palm Beach County Summer Golf Croquet League, which will begin its ninth season of play in July. The league offers competitive opportunities to players of all ability levels, along with instruction and practice opportunities. All league activities will be held at the National Croquet Center, 700 Florida Mango Road, West Palm Beach. Team matches will be played on two nights weekly for five weeks beginning July 11. One league plays on Tuesday evenings, the other on Wednesday. Teams choose their level of play: beginner or championship. On Aug. 15, final playoff games will be held between the top teams in each division. The league has grown in popularity since its inception and last season, 88 teams competed, drawing players from as far north as Martin County and as far south as Boca Raton. Practice sessions will take place from 1-3 p.m. on four Saturdays: June 17, June 24, July 1 and July 8. The league will be capped at 98 teams. Teams must select a team name and sign up a roster of two to four players. Costs are $40 per player for two-player teams; $30 per player for three-player teams and $25 per player for four-player teams.   \n<!-- map content:  Melania Trump will move to the White House this summer. Despite reports over the past few months speculating otherwise, the first lady will join President Donald Trump in their new residence after their son, Barron, completes his school year. &raquo; Trump&rsquo;s Easter: Twitter, church, brunch, egg hunt, wheels-up to D.C. &raquo; COMPLETE COVERAGE: President Donald Trump in Palm Beach &ldquo;That has always been the plan, so yes it&rsquo;s true,&rdquo; Stephanie Grisham, communications director for the first lady, said in an email Monday when asked to confirm reports from several news outlets that Melania and Barron will move to Washington, D.C., this summer. &raquo; Melania Trump visits girls at HomeSafe in Lake Worth The first lady&rsquo;s plans have been no secret, with officials saying in November that she and Barron would continue to live at Trump Tower in New York until Barron completed his current schoolyear. But since the president took office in January, several news outlets have speculated on whether she would remain in New York throughout the presidency. One widely shared US Weekly article cited &ldquo;a family insider&rdquo; as saying Melania Trump was considering staying in Trump Tower. &ldquo;Separate lives,&rdquo; the magazine&rsquo;s mid-February cover read. &raquo; White House releases official portrait of first lady Melania Trump &ldquo;Melania goes back and forth and once Barron finishes school, it&rsquo;s hard to take a child out of school with a few months left, she and Barron will be moving over to the White House,&rdquo; the president countered in a news conference soon after US Weekly&rsquo;s story was published. The Town Council reappointed Scotch Peloso as a regular voting member and Daniel McDonnell was promoted from an alternate to a regular member. Newcomer Rosemary Carpenter was selected as an alternate and Donald Scott retained his seat as an alternate. The seven-member board hears cases involving violations of the town&rsquo;s code and ordinances. Members can impose fines and penalties. A seat opened after Madelyn Greenberg completed her three terms as a regular member. Peloso, a tutor at Palm Beach International Academy in Boca Raton, has been on the board for a year. He was a real estate investor for 10 years, according to his application. &ldquo;I feel that I bring a reasonable and rational point of view that also wishes to preserve the small town character of Palm Beach where I grew up,&rdquo; he wrote in his application. &ldquo;My 40 years of experience of witnessing the changes in Palm Beach brings a unique perspective to the board.&rdquo; McDonnell, who worked in administrative management for two financial services firms, had been an alternate for six months. He has served on the Recreation Advisory Commission and the Centennial Commission and as a liaison for the mayor at City of West Palm Beach meetings. &ldquo;I think it&rsquo;s very important to this town,&rdquo; he said of the code board. &ldquo;The codes are important. The standards are important.&rdquo; Carpenter is a retired corporate attorney. &ldquo;Most of my life I&rsquo;ve been working to ensure laws and regulations are complied with,&rdquo; she told the council. -->\n<article class=\"story cm-channel-story cm-story cm-image\">\n\t    <a href=\"/news/local/palm-beach-town-council-appoints-code-board-members/u5v4kFjaHvwZ6JoQvv6BoM/\" class=\"story-photo-link\" target=\"\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<figure>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<img src=\"/rf/image_inline/Pub/p8/PalmBeachDailyNews/2017/04/17/Images/newsEngin.18427732_brazilian-court-fine-windows.jpg\" title=\"Palm Beach Town Council appoints code board members \" alt=\"Palm Beach Town Council appoints code board members \">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<span class=\"\"></span>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t</figure>\n\t\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"story-tease-content\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<h3 class=\"story-title\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<a href=\"/news/local/palm-beach-town-council-appoints-code-board-members/u5v4kFjaHvwZ6JoQvv6BoM/\" target=\"\">Palm Beach Town Council appoints code board members </a>\n\t\t\t\t\t</h3>\n\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t        <p class=\"story-byline\">\n    \n\t    by\n\t\t\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\t\n\t\t\n\t\n\t\n\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t  \n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t \n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t \n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\nAleese Kopf, <span class=\"story-source\">Daily News Staff Writer</span>\n\t</p>\n<div class=\"story-text cm-truncate\" style=\"word-wrap: break-word; visibility: visible;\"><div>Four residents were appointed to the town’s Code Enforcement Board last week.    1419#] /Pub/p8/PalmBeachDailyNews/2017/04/17/Stories/newsEngin.17049724.xml [ConcreteProxyImpl:EOM::CompoundStory, 2.0.2050531192] -->\n        <!-- cacheScope: ContextMap[_rootContainerContextMap:ContextMap[primaryCategory:/Online/Home, sectionId:/]] -->\n        <!-- cacheScope type: class com.eidosmedia.portal.render.ctx.ContextMap -->\n        <!-- noRootContainer:  -->\n    \n \n    \n    \n    \n    \n    \n                        \n    \n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\n    \n    \n    \n        \n        \n        \n        \n        \n        \n        \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n     \n\n\n        \n            \n            \n                \n                \n                \n                \n                \n                \n\n\t            \n\t               \n\t                \n\t                \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                    \n\t                    \n\t                \n\t                \n\t                \n\t            \n\n                \n            \n        \n    \n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n    \n    \n        \n            \n        \n        \n            \n            \n            \n            \n                \n            \n        \n    \n\n\n\n    \n    \n    \n    \n    \n    \n    \n    \n    \n    \n    \n        \n        \n        \n        \n            \n            \n            \n\t\t    \n        \n        \n    \n<!-- map content:  Dozens of coastal communities have passed resolutions supporting plastic bag bans, and local students want Palm Beach to be the next. North End resident Gray Foster, a ninth-grader at Palm Beach Day Academy, plans to make a case for a plastic ban Thursday during a meeting of the town&rsquo;s Ordinances, Rules and Standards Committee. &ldquo;Palm Beach is probably the most famous coastal town in Florida, known for its beautiful homes and pristine beaches, but like every coastal community our incredible lifestyle comes with a responsibility to our ocean,&rdquo; Foster wrote in a report to the committee. &ldquo;One of the greatest threats to our oceans and its creatures is plastic bags and balloons.&rdquo; Town officials asked the Day Academy several weeks ago to research the effects of balloons and single-use bags on the environment. &ldquo;The environmental impact from balloons and plastic is something the future generations will have to deal with, especially in coastal communities, so we are hopeful that by engaging our children today it will pay dividends in the future as tough policy decisions are made,&rdquo; said Deputy Town Manager Jay Boodheshwar. &ldquo;I think Gray&rsquo;s report is excellent. His research was thorough and his conclusions were to the point.&rdquo; The committee will use Foster&rsquo;s report when members discuss banning outdoor balloons and regulating plastic bags. Environmentalists have shown that plastic clogs landfills and storm sewers, pollutes beaches and oceans, and poisons marine life. &ldquo;After one use, retail plastic bags usually become unsightly litter, a nuisance to our town crews, dangerous to our marine life and toxic to our environment and Palm Beach needs to take a stand on the issue,&rdquo; Foster wrote. &ldquo;The release of balloons is simply purposeful littering and should not be tolerated either.&rdquo; Balloons The Juno-based Loggerhead Marinelife Center has been working on a multi-county balloon ban initiative for more than a year. The center has successfully convinced several cities and towns in Martin, Palm Beach, Broward and Miami-Dade counties to ban balloons. Conservationists at the center say they commonly treat sea turtles that have ingested deflated balloons after mistaking them for jellyfish, a common prey. Florida statute already makes it unlawful for people to intentionally release balloons into the atmosphere. If they do, there&rsquo;s a $250 fine. But the town could take it a step further and prohibit residents from using balloons outdoors. &ldquo;Plastic pollution and balloons continue to be one of the most significant threats impacting marine life in coastal communities around the globe,&rdquo; Tommy Cutt, LMC chief conservation officer, wrote in an email Tuesday. &ldquo;The Town of Palm Beach is home to important sea turtle habitat and relies heavily on tourism through seaside resorts. Banning balloons or plastic bags is a proactive approach to reduce pollution, protect marine life and keep the island&rsquo;s beaches clean &mdash; which in turn helps support the local economy.&rdquo; Plastic bags Unlike a balloon ban, local governments in Florida don&rsquo;t have the authority to ban plastic bags. In 2008, the state passed legislation preventing local governments from regulating plastic bags. It also required the Department of Environmental Protection to submit a report on the &ldquo;necessity and efficacy&rdquo; of plastic bag regulation. The report, released in 2010, introduces many options for discouraging the use of plastic bags. But until the legislature adopts the DEP recommendations, local governments don&rsquo;t have control. In the past two years, various House and Senate bills have been introduced unsuccessfully. Opponents say a ban would be expensive for stores and for consumers and would create job losses. &ldquo;All bills addressing plastic bags have died in committees because there are some special interests fighting to protect the profits on plastic bags,&rdquo; Foster wrote. &ldquo;The slick talking points of the pro-plastic bag lobby are not convincing when we have a front-row seat to the damage they do here in our own town. The young people of Palm Beach are counting on adults to do anything they can to preserve the beauty and quality of life here in our hometown and to follow through with the responsibilities we are reminded of each time we admire the Atlantic Ocean that makes our lives here so unique.&rdquo; Foster said a resolution from the town to the Florida Legislature is the most effective way to address the issue &ldquo;for the time being.&rdquo; Several other coastal towns already have enacted resolutions seeking the ability to regulate plastic bags, he said. In November, California became the first state to ban single-use plastic bags at most grocery stores. -->\n<article class=\"story cm-channel-story cm-story cm-image\">\n\t    <a href=\"/lifestyles/environment/palm-beach-student-encourages-town-ban-plastic-balloons-bags/Ve6GboWpvC5V24C2ljIHrM/\" class=\"story-photo-link\" target=\"\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<figure>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<img src=\"eom:/ustrings/newsengin-17049724-\" title=\"Palm Beach student encourages town to ban plastic balloons, bags \" alt=\"Palm Beach student encourages town to ban plastic balloons, bags \">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<span class=\"\"></span>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t</figure>\n\t\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"story-tease-content\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<h3 class=\"story-title\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<a href=\"/lifestyles/environment/palm-beach-student-encourages-town-ban-plastic-balloons-bags/Ve6GboWpvC5V24C2ljIHrM/\" target=\"\">Palm Beach student encourages town to ban plastic balloons, bags </a>\n\t\t\t\t\t</h3>\n\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t        <p class=\"story-byline\">\n    \n\t    by\n\t\t\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\t\n\t\t\n\t\n\t\n\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t  \n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t \n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t \n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\nAleese Kopf, <span class=\"story-source\">Daily News Staff Writer</span>\n\t</p>\n<div class=\"story-text cm-truncate\" style=\"word-wrap: break-word; visibility: visible;\"><div>Dozens of coastal communities have passed resolutions supporting plastic bag bans, and local students want Palm Beach to be the next. North End resident Gray Foster, a ninth-grader at Palm Beach Day Academy, plans to make a case for a plastic ban Thursday during a meeting of the town’s Ordinances, Rules and Standards Committee.
